<Author>Markmmg
<Content>Nice, but I will not stay here again. The location of the hotel is great. It is easy to get to since it is located on Canal St. and it is located just on the edge of the French Quarter. While the hotel is nice, the rooms are very small for the rate that they charge. I wasn't too impressed with the quality of the rooms either. We found little black hairs on some of the wash cloths and the hotel shampoo was left over from the previous guest. The parking was absolutely horrible. To start with, they charge you $30 to park your car at the hotel and valet is the only option. When we parked, we were told to call down 15 minutes ahead of time to get the car. Well, when we were checking out, they told us that we had to go down to the lobby and wait in line for 30 minutes to give them out parking stub so that they could retrieve our car, which took another 20 minutes. It was a 50 minute ordeal to get our car. The parking area was completely crazy with close to 100 people trying to get their cars. There are just too many other hotels in New Orleans with better rates, better comparable rooms, and trememdously better parking accomodations for me to ever stay here again. I expected much better from a Marriott hotel.

<Author>bluefog
<Content>Mixed Opinion Our 3 night stay was enjoyable, with the exception of a few items that seem to plague the expensive hotels.CONS:- Parking. We dislike valet parking due to the inconvenience (little access to car, wait time, etc.), not the price. There is no option except valet parking here.- Internet. Excessive fee ($15) and they don't even have wireless access.- Elevators. They claim to be more efficient (touch your floor number outside, then you are assigned an elevator that goes to that floor, no buttons on the inside). But they aren't. As an example: On 3 occasions, we entered our floor number, assuming we'd be assigned to the elevator that was sitting right there at the lobby level, open and ready to go. Instead, we were assigned the elevator that was at the highest floor, which we had to wait for (you can see where the elevators are located when you enter your floor number).- Food options. Over priced and limited selection at breakfast, but the restaurant seemed to be a decent place for dinner.We don't understand why the big hotels will nickel and dime you for parking and internet.PROS:- Comfortable room, although a little small (but that's expected from a downtown hotel in a big city).- Excellent location and friendly staff.Would return to this hotel, but not for the price that we paid.

<Author>JoeytravelerNJ
<Content>Busy Hotel We stayed here for 2 nights as part of an escorted tour group. The hotel location is great, it sits on the edge of the French Quarter and is in walking distance from the French Quarter, Harrahs Casino, Jackson Square, Bourbon St, many shops  restaurants. The street cars are right outside the main entrance. This is a very busy hotel with a large lobby which is often quite loud. They have a large lobby bar in the center, a nice restaurant on the side, some shops in the back, an ATM, two airline check-in kiosks  a concierge desk. The elevator system is different from others, in order to call for one you must enter the floor number you are going to, it will then tell you which elevator to use. It's very efficient. There are 2 wings to the hotel and 2 sets of elevators. Our room was high on the 24th floor with a nice view of the city. It wasn't an overly large room but the queen beds were extremely comfortable with lots of pillows, a big flat screen tv, coffee/tea maker - no room safe. The bathroom was very nice with good quality soap, shampoo, lotion,  conditioner. We were in the opposite wing of the fitness  business center, so I had to go down to the lobby, get to the other set of elevators then go up to the fitness center. The fitness center was minimal at best with some treadmills, step climbers, machines,  free weights. They are housed in two small rooms with nice views of the city. They have a water cooler, towels,  headphones to use for free. There is no locker room, no sauna,  no indoor pool which was all disappointing for a large Marriott hotel not to have. The business center is pretty good with free internet pcs along with business supplies like paper, post-it notes, pens, paper clips, scotch tape  printers. We had the buffet breakfast each morning and the food and staff were wonderful. They had a huge variety of choices at the buffet and the food was very tasty. They prepared eggs any way you asked them to and also made fresh waffles - they were great! The staff at this hotel is extremely accomadating and friendly, they'll go out of their way to help you out and that was a nice surprise for such a large hotel. The staff is definitely the hotels greatest asset.  
<Date>Nov 12, 2008

<Author>travelori
<Content>Great stay! My husband and I stayed here for Voodoo fest, and stayed October 23-27. We normally try to book the older, boutique hotels in the Quarter, but the price Marriott was offering for the Voodoo fest ($125/night) was far better than anything else we could find. Overall, excellent experience with this hotel.Check-in: Quick and easy. We arrived around 9:30PM, and were unpacking in our room within 10 minutes. Signed out a safe deposit box later for our passports, extra cash and other things we didn't want to lose.Room #3915: Somewhat small/cramped, but otherwise nice. Decor is up-to-date; view is opposite the Mississippi and looks out over Canal, all the way to the lake. I think this was the highest floor. Despite that fact, the elevators were pretty quick.Bed: In a word: Luxurious. Incredibly soft, cushy and comfy. After walking around all day at the festival, this bed was heavenly!Bath: Plenty of towels, hot water, and the ammenities are really nice. The lotion had a nice, gingery citrus scent that isn't too feminine or masculine. Just right. Shower head might be a bit low for anybody over 5' 9. I had to crouch a bit to rinse my hair.Housekeeping: Room always done up by the time we arrived back from our daily excursions. No problems here.Wireless Internet: Was a bit disappointed at being charged $15 a day, as so many hotels offer this free nowadays, but whatever. The tech support was the best I've ever experienced through a hotel though. I had some problems with my wireless card accepting the hotel's, and the 1-800 tech line was able to walk me through the steps to enable it. A real live person, no less.Bar: Had a drink at the bar downstairs -- they make a mean dirty martini! Prices were fairly normal for a hotel bar - about $8 each (and they didn't skimp on the alcohol).Would stay here again without hesitation. Only reason I didn't give it the highest rating was because the room is so darn small. Almost too small for two people to get around in comfortably. However, we had no plans to stay in the room for long anyway, so it didn't pose too big an issue for our stay.

<Author>mickir
<Content>Great Location! Great Hotel! My husband and I spent 4 nights at the Canel Street Marriott in mid-August (a week before Gustav). He was attending a convention. We were originally booked for the Doubletree, but after looking at the reviews on Trip Advisor, we moved over to this hotel. Wow! we were so glad that we did! We got a cheaper rate and a fantastic room. We requested a corned king-size room and were not disappointed. The front desk staff worked to ensure we got exactly what we wanted... a corner room on the 31st floor overlooking the river.... at no added costs!The room was large and very comfortable. Great service overall. The elevators are great! and really quick! Add to this a terrific location and it made our trip very memorable. I was very surprised how friendly and fun New Orleans was. My husband and I are in our early 50s, so we we're really into Bourbon Street, but we enjoyed walking through the French Qtr, going to the casino (Harrah's is really nice!), and eating outstanding food (NOLA was good and Palace Cafe was excellent). I highly recommend New Orleans and the Canel Street Marriott. I know I'm looking forward to going back!

<Author>ElaineNY
<Content>Best location for everything My husband and I had a terrific 4 day stay at the Marriott. It is centrally located and accessible to everything, either by foot or streetcar. The rooms are quite small, but clean and well-kept. We arrived very early, about 9 A.M., but were given our room immediately. The restaurant 555 has excellent food. I was quite surprised for a hotel restaurant to have such tasty local food. I had my first oysters there (grilled) and they were so good! The people working at the Marriott couldn't have been more helpful. We arrived in the rain, and they made suggestions for us to get through the day, with wonderful directions. Really nice staff. I definitely will go back to New Orleans. It is a beautiful state with some terrific people. You can't go wrong with the Marriott. While it isn't fancy, you can walk to the river, French Quarter, Bourbon Street, Cafe du Monde (yummy doughnuts), Harrah's, Riverwalk, etc. If you prefer there are 3 streetcar lines that are nearby to continue your tour of the city. We are going back next year!!!

<Author>madhattertx
<Content>The best hotel I have stayed at in New Orleans I can honestly say I will not stay at another hotel when I return to New Orleans other than this one. From the moment I arrived, I was blown away with almost every aspect of the hotel. The valets were courteous to us when they took our rental car and everytime we dealt with them to go out/return. The 555 restaurant was extremely good. They had the best omelet bar and eggs benedict I have ever enjoyed. The breakfast buffet is pricey, but was extremely good. The service was excellent. I admit we did not try them for anything other than breakfast.Check-in: Very professional and customer service oriented. We arrived very early from the airport (10am) and were able to immediately get a very nice room on the 22nd floor. The lobby is very large and relaxing. The artwork was wonderful and the center bar area was very appealing. My only issue would be with the concierge service. Every single time we asked her for assistance, she was on the phone with what seemed like personal calls. uh, huh...ok, I have somebody here...I'll call you right back. She seemed bored with customers and didn't smile really at all. Concierge is a key position for the hotel and I think they could do better. The hotel has elevators that operate by typing in your floor number on a keypad and then being assigned a specific elevator by alphabetical letter. I found this very pleasant because we didn't have to all crowd into the first available elevator and be forced to stop at a variety of floors. Very well done, Marriott.The room: The room had very nice everything...Nice tv, great river view, nice bedding and a nice bathroom. My only issue was with the mattress pads which were slightly uncomfortable and had an overwhelming tendency to slip off the mattress...which also had a tendency to slip off the boxspring. The room was well insulated from noise issues except on our last night (Saturday night/Sunday morning) when we were awakened at 2:20am by drunken 20-somethings (I hope not teens) having a yelling match outside our door in the hallway. We came that close to calling security.Speaking of these 20-somethings...we think we encountered them again the next morning when one of them was yelling at a valet and acting like a fool because their car was left on the driveway instead of being parked in the garage, which was full by the time they returned to the hotel after their evening of stupidity from the night before. Listen...being in your 20s and having your family's money doesn't entitle you to be a jerk and a waste to society. No number of tattoos or an emo haircut is going to make you look cool either. Check-out...well I am still checking on a problem because we had to split the bill, but the desk clerks were professional.A warning...beware of taxi drivers at night in New Orleans because they are hit or miss. We had one who treated us right and didn't overcharge us and we had one who insisted on trying to pick up 2 more people to share our cab because our group of 3 wasn't enough to fill his van cab. Would he have charged us all the same fare for different destinations? We ended up not being able to get other riders (oh, darn) and the cab driver ended up overcharging us by $8 because...and he said it...he missed out on making his usual rate for carrying 5 passengers at all times.

<Author>Peaceloveweeniedogs
<Content>Just Right! My best friend and I stayed at the New Orleans Marriot this weekend. It was great. The location is great you can get on all 3 trolleys within a block of the hotel. The french quarter is on one side of the hotel and Harrah's casino is a block down on the other side. We got our room for $89 through travelzoo though we enjoyed the room enough to pay full price. Though the special said King bed with no view we were given 2 queens with a view of Harrah's, the bridge and the Mississippi. Like other posters we agree the beds were AWESOME! The hotel has it's own parking garage so you just pull in and they park your car and unload your stuff, so easy. When we walked into the hotel two people were set up to direct you to check in. The lobby is very smart. The middle is a big lounge area with a bar at the end. People used that area for many things- some were working or using laptops, some were waiting or relaxing, some were snacking/drinking/talking. As far as our room size, I think the room size was average and the decor very tasteful. We ate the breakfast buffet in the hotel 5fifty5 restaurant. As lovers of breakfast we thougt it was very good but it would be pricey for a whole family. The concierge was nice and helpful and gave us dinner recommendations. We ate at Bourbon House which is just past Acme Oyster. She recommended Acme but the line was long so moved on and ate at Bourbon. The food was good and seafood especially the oysters tasted really fresh. You call the parking garage 5 minutes before you leave and they pull your car and have it waiting for you. And they put a ice cold bottle of water in the cup holder, nice touch. Oh, and the shampoo, etc was citrus and also a nice touch. I like to travel so when planning a getaway first I decide my budget and then the area I want to be in. Then look for hotels with comfy beds and great location. This hotel met all my travel criteria. For me this hotel's beds were equivalent to the Pan Pacific in SanFrancisco (and that says alot)! Happy Travels!!

<Author>speechcreature
<Content>New Orleans Marriott--a Great Location! The NO Marriott is located on Canal Street, between Decater and Royal (or close to Royal anyhow). I had never been to New Orleans before, so I didn't realize what a great location that really was. I didn't actually pick it--I was placed there after winning a bid on Priceline. Canal, as it turns out, divides Uptown from the French Quarter. It was so convenient for me to just walk out the door and be able to walk down the street to the FQ (Bourbon Street, all the antique shops, great music, dance, restaurants) as well as to go across the street to catch the street car (which took me into the Garden District). Turning left out the door, I was quickly able to get to the end of Canal Street, where you can take a free ferry to Algiers. The hotel was very clean, nice lobby for people watching, and staff was friendly and helpful in terms of helping me ( I was vacationing solo, so they provided excellent travel tips). My room was on the small side, but it was cute, and had a king bed. It was billed as a 4 star, but I'd say it was more of a 3 star type accommodation. I did not eat at the restaurant because there were so many places that had been recommended in the FQ, but they did have one. I also did not use the bar area, but it had tons of seating, and many others were chatting there. While I was there, there was a convention for the National Association for the Deaf, so people were signing all over the place--it was a VERY quiet week. The pool was nice, and it felt good to cool off in the afternoon after sight seeing in 104 humid weather. Because the pool is outdoors, and it is between towers (which block the sun), you only get direct tanning rays for a few hours in the afternoon as far as I could tell, but it was enough to turn me golden brown over the course of my 4 day stay. I would be very disappointed if I returned to the city and Priceline placed me anywhere but there. I'll be keeping my fingers crossed while they do their search that the Marriott NO comes up when I return to NO in the future, which I certainly plan to!  
<Date>Jul 15, 2008

<Content>Pretty Good Experience We stayed here in May '08 during the Conference USA baseball tournament at Tulane University. We wanted to be in the French Quarter but also close to the streetcar line that could take us to Tulane. As it turns out, the streetcar is NOT a good way to get to Tulane's baseball facility. It's convenient to both the French Quarter and to Harrah's Casino. <Author>tamstrat
<Content>Overall nice experience My husband and I recently were in NOLA for a business convention and stayed at this Marriott property for 3 days. This hotel is in downtown New Orleans and is within a few blocks of The French Quarter. I liked the fact that it was within walking distance of pretty much everything we wanted to see and do, yet not right on Bourbon Street where all the music and people partying stay.There is shopping and restaurants galore nearby, some high end shops such as Saks Fifth Avenue were a couple of blocks down on Canal Street and of course just a few blocks from The French Quarter, so there is plenty to eat, drink and shop nearby. The location of this hotel was perfect for us.The room we had was nothing special, not bad at all, just nothing to knock you out. Typical Marriott hotel room. We were on the 28th floor and there was a nice view of Canal street, the downtown area and further down, the Mississippi River. The housekeeping staff did a good job of keeping the room clean and well appointed. This is a large hotel, and others on this site have commented about how well the elevators work to serve the towers. Personally we had several bad experiences waiting and waiting and waiting for the elevators. To be fair however, there was a huge convention going on and the lobby was packed night and day, maybe if it weren't so busy there wouldn't be this problem, but it was a bit of a hassle waiting upwards of 10 minutes for an elevator, and I am not exaggerating, that is how long I waited at one point.There is a Starbucks in the lobby and also a restaurant (which we did not eat at). Also, there is a bar in the lobby that was consistently crowded with people attending the convention. You can get sushi and appetizers here. The service at the desk (check in, concierge, bellman, etc) were all very nice and pleasant. The service in the lobby bar was terrible I have to say. Drinks were not refilled and servers were no where to be found. Maybe since Katrina they are having trouble staffing? I don't know, but that was a little annoying. Here are all these people with an open tab at the bar, ready, willing and able to spend MONEY and no one was around to take orders. Kind of not a good business move, but overall everyone else we encountered at this hotel went out of their way to help and make our stay enjoyable.I would recommend this hotel to anyone wanting to stay near the French Quarter in NOLA and if I ever return there I'm sure I would stay here again.  
<Date>May 23, 2008

<Author>Brian_NVA
<Content>Functional As others have pointed out, this is kind of a typical downtown highrise hotel, nothing special except the location near the French Quarter. Even though a sign said I was on the Marriott Rewards Elite Floor, the room and hallway decor was pretty unremarkable... older furnishings and somewhat drab decor. Perfectly suitable for a business trip, though, which is why I was staying there.One rather interesting thing... This is the first hotel I have ever stayed in where the elevator buttons are on the outside of the elevator. You push the buttons in the elevator lobby for the desired floor, a display tells you which elevator is going to be yours, and then that elevator comes and takes you to your floor. I wonder how many people did like me and got on the elevator, only to discover there are no floor buttons on the inside! I liked my view from Room 1910... nice partial view of the mighty Mississippi, with a cruise ship, ferries, riverboats, and freighters winding their way up and down the river. The bathroom was small... overall the room and bathroom would have been tight for more than one occupant. As usual for Marriott, the bed and shower head were both nice. Room service was mediocre... it had pretty much cooled off by the time it got to me.One pet peeve... the combination alarm clock and IPOD player is a nice thought, but absolutely indecipherable when it came to setting either the time or the alarm. Front desk was no help with this, either. I needed my kids there.

<Content>Great Location, Small rooms We took a 5 day weekend in New Orleans. It was our first visit there. The Hotel location was super. The lounge was nice but I did not check out the restaurants. Very small room and very small bathroom. The health club was open 24 hours, but the pool was closed for repairs. I would have no problem staying there again.

<Author>BDPHD
<Content>Great Stay--No Problems! Stayed in New Orleans Marriott for a conference that overlapped Mardi Gras. I was a little worried that all the Mardi Gras craziness would affect the hotel's cleanliness, service, etc.--not so. Our room was ready on time and to specifications. Not very big, but I have stayed in smaller rooms. Bed was very comfortable, and housekeeping was attentive and responded to special requests. All the staff was always friendly and helpful.The room itself was nicer than the Sheraton across the street. I would certainly stay here again. It has a great location straddling the French Quarter and CBD. You can take a cab or shuttle from the airport and never need a car. My gripes:* Internet from the room was so costly. I know this is typical of this kind of hotel, but really $10 is excessive.* Bar in the lobby was WAY overpriced.* Food in the hotel was not great--but really folks, it's New Orleans, do not eat in your hotel!!Otherwise, it was a nice stay. Nothing special, but very good. Take the St. Charles Streetcar for a day trip to the Garden District!

<Content>Great front desk  some lapses in housekeeping I stayed in this hotel during a convention. The location is good for visiting the French Quarter. Check in at the front desk was very efficient, and when I asked for a room with a view I was given a very nice corner room that looked over the river and the French Quarter. I have heard that NO is very short on workers, so I figured that my housekeeper was probably overworked and underpaid and still left a tip.We found the bellmen extremely helpful and cheerful. I am most thankful.One more note. Try to eat at Mr. B's Bistro, which is only a short walk away. The food is fabulous!

<Author>jcoltrane
<Content>Cramped Quarters, Nice Location Stayed here for one night on a great Priceline rate ($60). Located right on the edge of the French Quarter, this hotel is an easy walk to any location in the Quarter, the Aquarium, the Casino, Riverwalk, Convention Center and anywhere that the casual visitor is likely to want to visit. The hotel is very recently renovated, with the attractive, contemporary lobby and fast elevators being the newest addition. (I honestly don't understand the confusion some reviewers have with the elevators... They are quite easy to use and insure that you don't have more than one stop on the way to your destination floor.) We were given a room on the 21st floor in the River tower that faced north, affording us a view of the other hotel tower. Not the best view, but at this price I'm not complaining. The room was clean and recently remodeled, with a bed spread that is a bit more garish than anything I would buy, but again... at this price, who's complaining?The room was small. Barely large enough to accommodate the bed, armoire and a small desk. Our pre-requested crib wasn't waiting for us when we checked in, but one was brought up within 20 minutes. Placing it in the room was a challenge. we fit it next to the window, but it was a struggle requiring the relocation of an ottoman and a small table.The staff were helpful and eager to assist with directions and any other issues. The valet parking is a bit overpriced ($30), but the valets were nice and helped loading and unloading bags.All in all it was a nice stay, but the room size could be a problem for anyone who really needs to spread out where they stay. We just viewed it as preparation for the future, as we were embarking on a cruise the next day in a ship's cabin that was even smaller.Very nice location for the traveler not seeking a quaint hotel in the Quarter. Claustrophobically-challenged travelers beware!

<Author>BoatNut2
<Content>If you're claustrophobic I wouldn't recommend it We stayed here for 4 nights. The first thing I would say is that you'd better pack light, since the rooms are SMALL. When I say small, I've stayed in Super 8's that have more room. Oh, did you want to use your computer on the internet? Prepare to shell out $15 a DAY. Again, Super 8's have FREE internet. If you drove a car, prepare to pay $30 a day for parking and then tip the valet to get your car. Now you've just added about $50 per day to your stay. Since the room is so small, you want to go down and have a drink at the bar? A Miller Genuine Draft and a vodka collins will set you back a mere $12.07 (and I didn't even get kissed). Unless you MUST stay here (I was attending a conference at the hotel, so I didn't have a choice) I wouldn't recommend it. For what you pay for the room...errr I mean big closet, the value just isn't there. I travel extensively for my job and stay in hotels an average of 80-90 nights per year and this place sits at the top of the list of Not Good places to stay.

<Author>SpreeBee
<Content>Great Stay The Marriott in NO was a great stay. The location was conveniently located near places such as the casino, Bourbon St and Preservation Hall. Being on the main road, it was very easy to take the cable cars and hail a taxi to the airport. The bed was comfortable and the sheets and comforter were soft.The hotel lobby was renovated this summer and was very attractive. Although we never ate at the 4 restaurants in the hotel, they seemed to be priced on par with the rest of the city.

<Content>Good experience here! Bourban St is only 2 blocks away. MANY souvenier shops, clubs, etc all along the areas, as well as more upscale jewelry and art shops a little further into the Fr. Qu.Harrah's Casino, the Riverwalk and the Conv. Center are also only a 15 min. walk away.There is a computer and printer next to the front desk to print off your airline boarding pass for free. Mine was a good overview with a great guide for someone on a tight schedule. It was a short 10 minute walk to the Grayline meeting place.The Front Desk is now on the first floor, along with a bar, coffee shop, small gift shop and the elevators were not confusing, just different from the norm.I hope to come back someday and would stay here again.

<Author>dolmatt
<Content>Marriott New Orleans-beautiful hotel with excellent location! My group consisted of 4 women under the age of 35, so above all, we wanted a hotel that was safe and close to everything-and the Marriott New Orleans exceeded all of our expectations!! Located on busy Canal st. just two very short blocks to Bourbon, we felt safe stumbling back to the hotel at 4 in the morning after too many Hurricane's at Pat O'Brien's-the streets were well lit and safe. The hotel itself was undergoing construction in the lobby, but it really didn't interfere with our stay. Our room was exceptionally clean, with the most amazing beds any of us have ever slept in-so comfortable! The staff were very accommodating and let us have a later check-out (without charge) since our flight was a little later in the day-very appreciated. Also, this hotel is a typical high-rise, luxury hotel, so if you are expecting to get old style New Orleans accommodations, this is not the hotel to pick, but it was definitely the one for us-and if the rates are good, it will always be the hotel we choose while staying in the beautiful city of New Orleans. As for the city of New Orleans, it was amazing-there is definitely fun to be had by everyone. We enjoyed the nightlife of Bourbon St, but we also enjoyed the ghost and cemetery tours offered-loved them!!! We had an amazing time. The people we met from New Orleans made our short time in the beautiful city a treat that we will cherish forever!! Can't wait to get back next year!!

<Author>EQ3282
<Content>Decent Hotel on the mend; Security better to interact with than most staff My GF booked this hotel on Priceline.com (pick your own rate), and we ended up getting the hotel for more than half off on a Saturday and Sunday night stay, which is a great deal! So, the value itself was good for the price we got. But, if we were to have payed the asking price, I am not sure it would have been worth it.We didn't have to deal with parking, as we left our car at a friend's place just outside of the city. But the motor port constantly looked busy, with cars going in and out.Needing a car was not necessary though, as the hotel is basically near just about anything. Its right on the edge of the French Quarter, a couple blocks away from the Riverfront (shopping, the Aquarium, Harrah's, a nice walk/jog locale), and a short train ride from the Superdome and 'downtown' NOLA. Getting a taxi is also not a problem either.The hotel is undergoing renovations (which were not mentioned beforehand). The major part is the lobby is being totally redone, so the bottom floor is basically a construction zone. As others have said, temporary front desks are in an area on the second floor.Check-in seemed to go OK, until we got to our room. The key cards weren't working. After we tried both numerous times, I went back down to get new ones. The gentleman at the desk was accusatory in tone, briskly saying, Do not hold them against credit cards or cell phones. That is why they do not work, when we did neither on the way up to the room. He said if the cards don't work a second time, use the wall phone near the elevators to call security, and they would let us in. I asked what we would do about the cards, and he simply said, We'll figure that out once it happens. Not so much an answer as a bumper.So, again, I trek back upstairs (interjection: the hotel elevators aren't as confusing as they seem or as they are described. You just punch in your floor and it tells you which elevator to take. NBD), and again the cards don't work. I go to the phone, call security, and they send someone up. The guard was very courteous and nice. Checked our IDs which was reassuring, and then tried out keys. Same results for him. He used his master to open the door and it worked fine. He said we could take the room and hope a new set works, or go down and switch rooms. We were meeting people, so we said we'd stick it out for now. He offered to bring us up a new set of keys, but after we told him we were heading out, he said just stop by the front desk, tell them we spoke to him, and they would give us a new set of keys. Asked us if there was anything else he could do, and thanked us for our patience.We stopped by the desk on our way out, got new keys from a different desk attendant (she seemed to care less when we told her the backstory re: security and such), and they finally worked (3rd time's the charm, I guess).Aside from the renovations, the interior of the hotel isn't too bad. Some new points (tiles, wall trim), and some old (carpeting). However, down in the 'lobby' area, it smells very musty and mildewy. Not overpowering, but a faint always-there scent.Our room was decent, albeit pretty typical. It was a bit on the small side, but it could be smaller. Definitely didn't feel cramped, at least. It was very clean, which was good. Even the bathroom was spotless. The bed was very comfortable, and the sheets were very nice. The down mattress topper was nice, but kept sliding around on the bed. The TV offered basic stations, but reception was spotty. The old model TV was a bit disapointing, but we didn't watch much TV anyway.Iron, ironing board, and internet router are avail (not sure if there's an internet charge or not). There's a coffee maker in the room too, with 2 bags decaf, one regular, and two tea bags (English tea and herbal). But, for all of that, there's only 2 sugars, 2 Sweet n Lows, and 2 half-and-half cuplets provided. A bit stingy, but I'm sure we could have gotten more had we called.The bathroom was a bit cramped, but manageable as long as only one person was in there at a time. The toilet wasn't very powerful, and backed-up a couple of times just from toilet paper. We did have to call once for a fix, left, and it was fine when we returned later that night.The AC in the room worked well, but seemed to putter out a bit at night (maybe regulated by the hotel). We set it at 68, and it maintained that during the day. But, at night, it'd get up to 72-73 at times.The windows are far from soundproof. Even on the 28th floor, we still heard motorcycles and bands playing the streets below. I felt bad for light sleepers on the lower floors. But, from the looks of it, they are replacing all the windows to be more soundproof. Might take them a while though.The view from the 28th floor was decent. We didn't have a 'river view' room, so we had a view of the French Quarter and up Canal St. Neither of which were particularly picturesque, but still not a bad sight.The Riverview Restaurant on the 41st floor looked nice, but we didn't eat there. We were going to have breakfast there one morning, but we saw signs that said it didn't open til 11am. Turns out it opens for breakfast much earlier. That's the hotel's fault for failure to inform properly.Instead, we went down to Perks, the coffee shop on the second floor. The menu is wide enough, esp. for coffee drinks. But, the service was very slow/unorganized. Otherwise, it wasn't too bad.Check out, as usual, was fine...just a call down to the front desk. But a final bill was not provided/slid under the door. The only bill was for 'extras', of which there were none during out stay.The hotel was busy while we were there, due to the AFL Championship game (I assume it was in the Superdome). However, never did the hotel feel crowded, which is very good.In all, nothing stands out, but nothing was that bad (aside from most staff interactions/service). So, a neutral rating for this neutral hotel on the brink of being very nice once renovations are completed. But again, due to the lower price we paid, it was a great value, if just for the location.

<Author>cruisermeg
<Content>Pool closed, lobby torn apart and the owners Refuse to notify guests! I was supposed to stay at this hotel on Canal Street for 3 nights at the end of June using a coupon for one of them. Arrived in N.O. La via Amtrak. I was advised to take a taxi to the hotel rather than the bus as, since Katrina, the buses in the area of the train station/arena/Superdome are irregular. There isn't much in the train station, but there is a Subway restaurant, some sort of coffee shop (which may be attached to the Subway), a small gift shop and both Amtrak and Greyhound ticket counters. A few police/sheriff's officers were present, and very polite and helpful in providing taxi info. My cab driver had just gotten his tax the day before. He lost everything in the storm. Very nice man. I can't believe that people in FEMA trailers have to pay rent on the space for the trailer. Don't get me started.Back to the hotel. Cabs to the hotels are a flat $11.00 (which includes a $1.00 fuel surcharge). Canal Street is under repair, as is much of the city, even two years after Katrina. Mostly the sidewalks are being rebuilt. I didn't have a problem with the construction in the city and I came down mainly because NOLa needs support.Upon arrival at the Marriott, I knew things were not going to be so swell. First, there were two uniformed associates outside, a doorman and a bellman. While one opened my door, neither of them got my bags out of the cab, nor did they offer a single female assistance into the hotel. Strike one. Upon entering, the entire lobby is under construction, so you have to lug your stuff up an escalator to the temporary lobby on the second floor. Let me explain. I have no problem with renovations. BUT, this hotel made NO mention of any renovations on their website. I checked and double checked, and called Marriott's Platinum desk and asked them to verify that no mention was made. There was nothing.I checked in. Actually, I was one day early but since the hotel was about 17% occupied, it wasn't a problem. I was given a room in the river tower with a view of the other tower and pool. The pools are closed for repair. Again, I was not informed of this in advance, nor at check-in! The Concierge lounge, access to which I receive due to my frequency of Marriott-branded use, was across the hotel resulting in a trip down the elevator, across the lobby and back up. Oh well.A side note about the elevators. Marriott seems to be adding fancy, high speed elevators to it's large hotels. The first I saw this was at the Marriott Marquis in NYC. You enter your desired floor on the keypad OUTSIDE the elevator. Then, the display returns the number/letter of the car which will take you to your floor. So, make sure you pay attention!Back to the hotel. The room was small with no view. The room was very noisy. I was told that all windows are being replaced with double-paned glass. Honestly, you can hear people whistling at other people on the street. Also, construction on the street starts at about 6:30 AM so forget about sleeping in. Again, I was up early and I don't have a problem with rebuilding. I took a walk through the hotel. Frankly, most of the associates didn't acknowledge anyone's presence. The sole person who convinced me to not leave was one of the security guards. She took it upon herself to escort me to the front desk for a room change. I was informed by several associates and managers that the owners of the hotel (it is my understanding that Marriott owns the people but others own the building) refused to inform guests of the renovations. This is inconceivable, especially given that the rate was $30 more per night than at the JW Marriott across the street and that property is completely renovated!I was upgraded to a two room suite. Actually a standard room with a connecting door into a parlor room. The living space was quite nice. I had two bathrooms, a dining area, couch, wet bar and there is a Murphy bed in the living room so I suppose it would be great for families, or to sell if the place is sold out. Not likely any time soon.The food and service in the concierge lounge wasn't great. OK, the first night, everything was seafood which I don't eat. Others may love it. There were mini crab cakes, shrimp and a big pot of gumbo. Problem is, the fishy smell overpowered the lounge, and the elevator landing outside. Fish shouldn't smell fishy or like garbage. It shouldn't really smell at all. Yuck! Also, for breakfast, the food was OK but there were no English Muffins, minimal pastries and cereals and just not a big selection. It looked nice, whatever there was of it. However, when I went to get butter balls for my toast, a piece of glass about 1 inch square was commingled with the butter and landed on my toast. I had to go into the little kitchen to find someone to show. Her response was, oh Ill take care of it. Not I'm sorry or some other words of concern, just Oh. Needless to say, breakfast that day, and each subsequent day was cafe au lait and beignets at Cafe du Monde. YUM!The restaurant is temporarily located on the 41st floor in what was the fine-dining restaurant pre-Katrina. There are a couple sandwiches, some entrees including fish and steak, and appetizers. But, dessert-wise, they had cheesecake, chocolate cake and ice cream. Come on. I know it's slow, but this is NOLa, can we at least have bread pudding or something yummy? The turkey club was good, albeit served just on run-of-the-mill white bread, not the advertised sourdough. When I saw that on the bar menu the second night, I asked the bartender. She said never in 20 years has it been on sourdough!Prices in the restaurant were reasonable for New Orleans. Typical hotel prices, although room service is around $2.00 per item more than the dining room, plus a 21% service charge and tax. That's a little too much if you ask me.Overall, the city is still almost empty which is a shame. I haven't been here for some 20 years and I don't recall too much. The French Quarter is indecent shape but there are a lot of vacant buildings. Also, while I remember lots of bars, I didn't remember seeing as many of the, hmm, adult-type places as I did this time.In conclusion, New Orleans needs support. It still can be a charming city again and I am sure that new developments (I saw a big TRUMP banner on the cab ride over) will help. y problems weren't with the city. Most of the people I encountered outside of the hotel were very nice. 80% of the people IN the hotel couldn't care less about whether guests are there. I wanted to shout..I came here to support the city, can you at least PRETEND you are glad I am here?? When I went to the desk to hand in my certificate, both the associate and manager told me I had to call in advance and that the certificate (a print out from the Marriott Rewards Platinum page that says PRINT THIS PAGE AND SURRENDER) was no good since it wasn't the certificate. Frankly I still don't know what they were saying, aside from implying that I am an idiot. So, after only 2 nights, I lugged my stuff down the escalator with no help, across the street and checked into the JW a day early. We shall see how THAT goes.I won return to the Marriott and I suggest they get their act together and inform people of the renovations. Out of all the associates I encountered, only two-a female security guard and the aforementioned bartender, were nice.

<Author>dgw9
<Content>Liked the New Orleans Marriott My wife and I stayed at the New Orleans Marriott from May 29-31st, 2007. It was our first trip to New Orleans and the ride from the Airport to the hotel was less than encouraging. I'm not talking about hurricane damage--the town is just fairly flat and uninspiring. Since the bus brought us around the back of the Marriott and then around to the front, it was still kind of discouraging. But when we got out and took a good look at the front of the hotel and then the inside, the Marriott did look pretty good. As others have mentioned, the hotel is undergoing renovation--not hurricane-related, I was told. As a result, the lobby is on the second floor, up a set of escalators. The renovations didn't have any effect on our stay except for the fact that we had to go up that escalator to the lobby and walk back to the our set of elevators to the Quarter Tower. Even though the 2nd floor lobby is temporary, it was done well. I can't speak for the restaurants at the hotel, but the breakfast and lunch buffets and snack service for the training classes was very good. The staff was nice, quick and knowledgeable.Housekeeping was in at 1:30 in the afternoon the first day and 11:30 the second day. Good job. Our 33rd floor room was clean and everything looked fine. The mattress was very good with a feather matress topper--very comfortable. Someone else wrote that Marriott changes comforter after every stay. Ours looked very fresh, so I believe it. The elevators and the system they use worked well except for the fact that I was at the hotel with 700 other people attending the same training, so at certain parts of the day there would be 100+ people waiting for the elevators at the same time. The line would clear quickly enough. Most of our elevator rides were very fast with very few stops. There is construction going on Canal Street--it looks like the City is replacing sidewalks all around. The construction started at 6:00 in the morning while we were there and it was easy to hear even on the 33rd floor. The sidewalk in front of the Marriott is done--they were working the other side of Canal, so any hotel in the area would have the same construction noise. There is a small bar on the 41st floor. Very expensive drinks and very few people. A waste of time and money. They have an internet-connected PC near the lobby. We were able to check-in with our airline and print our boarding passes for our return flight. That was free and very easy to navigate. The French Quarter is close by- I'd guess that where Bourbon Street starts at Canal is maybe 500 feet away. The French Quarter was everything they say it is, even though we were not there on the weekend.If you are going to the French Quarter, wear some decent shoes. My wife wore cheap sandals with very smooth soles. The French Quarter has a lot of granite and slate walks and when they are wet they were slippery. I saw a bunch of people slipping here and there. So make sure your sandals and shoes have good traction in case it rains. In closing, this Canal Street Marriott was a worthwhile place to stay while visiting the French Quarter.  
<Date>Jun 1, 2007

<Content>Good location , but some problems Booked 3 rooms three months ago through American Express Travel. Requeted an upper floor with a river view. I also emailed them a week before our arrival asking for a river view again. When we arrived we discovered the lobby and the lobby bar had been moved to the 2nd floor because of construction. It was too late to change our rooms at this point. The next morning we went up to the 41st floor for breakfast. We ordered coffee and waited 20 minutes for the waitress to bring it to us. The restaurant was almost empty so it was not because they were busy waiting on other guets. The beds are very comfortable and the location is very good so that is why we stay at the Marriott whenever we visit New Orleans.  Next year I think I will book the Hyatt, Hilton or the Sheraton. They are just as close to the French Quarter and I'll take a chance that their service will be better than what we received last week.

<Author>leaguecitytraveller
<Content>Great - Stayed Here for JazzFest My husband and I stayed at the New Orleans Marriott the last weekend of April for the Jazz Festival. The lobby is beautiful - crystal chandelier, dark wood desks and counters. The people at the check-in counter, bell hop station, and information desk were all friendly and professional. The rooms were clean and the bed linens were modern, clean, colorful. A/C worked great. The bathroom was ok - they need to install hand towel racks by the sink. The location is really great - a few blocks from the French Quarter and the shuttle bus to the Jazz Fest is just a couple of blocks down at the Sheraton. All in all, it was a good stay.

<Content>Never again My husband was going to a conference at the New Orleans Marriott, so we decided to stay there for the five nights of the conference. My husband booked our rez over the phone w/ the Marriott agent. He gave them the dates and they e-mailed a confirmation. A week or so later, I reviewed the confirmation e-mail and noticed that it was for only the first three nights, not for all five. When we called back, they said they were sold out the final two nights. So in the middle of our stay, we had to change hotels.When we arrived in N.O., we showed the confirmation e-mail to the cab driver to show him where we were staying. There was NO ADDRESS on the confirmation letter, and 3 Marriotts in N.O. So we had to guess which one was ours, causing needless anxiety.When we checked in, they told us there was construction going on between 9 and 5 every day, so we might experience some noise. No one had warned us about that when we booked! The desk person had a solution though: Since the work was being done on rooms between the 7th and 17th floors, she'd put us on the 8th floor. (Huh?)When we pointed out her faulty logic, she put us on the 29th floor. It was the dinkiest bathroom imaginable, with no towel racks for hand towels, and no bathroom fan, so the mirror fogged up after every shower.Outside our room, the hotel temp was kept so cold that one of the workshops my husband attended had to take a break so everyone could go back to their rooms for sweaters and jackets. And Marriott touts itself as a green business!Also during our stay, which was during JazzFest, (a huge tourist draw, when, presumably the hotel was at peak occupancy) the Marriottl closed down the in-hotel Starbucks for remodeling, so we had to cross Canal Street to go to the Sheraton for coffee drinks other than just straight coffee. And BTW, the cafe in the Marriott charges $14 for a bowl of hot cereal! (This isn't room service...this is a cafe.)

<Author>stlroadtraveler
<Content>Great Location and Great Experience I stayed 4 nights at the Marriott for a conference and was pleasantly surprised. I arrived mid morning from the airport and was immediately checked in and able to go to my room. It was nicely furnished and very comfortable. Probably the best hotel bed and mattress I've ever slept on. Although the bathroom was on the small side, it was very clean and well supplied. As previously mentioned by other guests, the new elevator system was different but easy to use. The only problem was the late afternoon, early evening when everyone was trying the access the elevators. It was as if the system was on overload - after waiting 15 mins, I walked down 12 flights of stairs (in heels - ouch!) and encountered many others doing the same. The cafe in the lobby was wonderful and had a great breakfast buffet with an omelet/waffle station and I thought the prices were very reasonable. The drinks in the lobby bar were pricey, but to be expected in the big city. Location is wonderful, everything is a easy walk (Riverwalk, Cafe de Monde, the Cathedral, French Market and Boubon Street). The meeting rooms (good temperature control - not too cold as most are) and food served for the conference were some of the best I've experienced. If I'm ever in New Orleans again I would certainly chose the Marriott.

<Author>Nash_Andrew
<Content>Excellent Location, Good Facilities Got a $60 per night rate at the Marriott last weekend (March 29 - April 1). The hotel couldn't have a better location: It's situated directly on Canal, two blocks from Bourbon Street and a few blocks from the river, casino, etc. The hotel itself showed no remaining ill effects from Katrina, and indeed everything was in good order. The rooms have been remodeled since the hurricane and featured the new Marriott style furnishings and bathroom fixtures. Revive bedding in place. Bathroom was very small, however, and the shower head was fit only for a midget (even my girlfriend found it too short). Some of the furniture, like the TV stand and desk, were clearly pre-renovation. Overall the room was very clean, comfortable, standard Marriott.Lobby didn't quite seem up to par with the rest of the hotel. I learned that there is a complete renovation of the lobby scheduled for this summer, however, so that should solve the problems there. The design schematics for this upgrade were on display in the lobby and looked very promising.Service was absolutely excellent. Very friendly and helpful all the way around. Everyone seemed genuinely happy to have us at the hotel. My only real complaint would be the $30 per day for parking. All in all, would stay again at the Marriott in a heartbeat, especially once they finish the common area renovations.

<Author>Superdocuk
<Content>Nice Hotel, Shame About the City I stayed in this hotel for four nights whilst attending a convention in New Orleans at the end of March. Overall the hotel met all my needs but my overall opinion is tainted by my major dislike of New Orleans.The Marriott is one of several in the chain to be found in New Orleans. This is the largest and sits on Canal Street. It is therefore very central to all the major attractions although Canal Street itself is lined by fairly tacky, cheap shops apart from a smart shopping mall at the southern end. The hotel is right on the edge of the French Quarter and a couple of blocks away from the riverside. It takes about 15mins to walk to the Convention Centre.Like many Marriotts it has a huge lobby with a cocktail bar in the centre. Check-in was friendly and speedy (and check-out even speedier). I was in the Quarter Tower. The new lift system is kind of funky. You select your floor before entering a lift and the computer system tells you which lift to take; and indeed you cannot change your selection once the lift comes.My room was a standard room with two queen-sized beds. The room itself was small and I would have preferred one bed and more floor space. All the rooms have been recently refurbished. I had a view from the 15th floor over the French Quarter and the Mississippi River. All the rooms seem to have a view. The bathroom was very well stocked with towels and the toiletries were nice. The room and bathroom were kept spotless throughout my stay. There was a coffee maker with adequate supplies including tea bags showing that the Americans don't understand the concept of boiling water being required to make tea properly. There is wired internet access at a daily price.The hotel has two outdoor pools side-by-side on the 5th floor roof surrounded by a sun deck. Neither appeared terribly appealing and colleagues reported the absence of changing rooms for the pool. There is also a fitness room but I did not see it.The bar was typically expensive as most hotel bars tend to be. The staff were decidely unfriendly when I visited and indeed bordered on being rude.There is cafe/restaurant and a gift shop off the lobby - the latter selling essential items. I did not eat in the restaurant as the convention supplied breakfast. The breakfast is an a la carte menu affair.Overall it is a good quality American Marriott and serves business guests well. I did not enjoy New Orleans and cannot see the attraction of it as a holiday destination but if you do, then the Marriott is ideally suited in terms of location but perhaps could do with better leisure facilities for tourists.  
<Date>Mar 29, 2007

<Author>takelson
<Content>Quality hotel, courteous staff My wife and I stayed at the Marriott from 2/9 tto 2/12. Our standard room on the 28th floor of the River Tower, facing the city, had a king bed. It was not the largest domestic hotel room we'd ever stayed in, but for a weekend trip it was fine. The furnishings were up to date, as was the bathroom. Everyone in the hotel, from check in to bell staff and housekeeping were friendly and courteous. We had booked through Amex Travel service, and our reservation included an upgraded room and breakfast. However, neither of these were noted in the hotel's reservation system. Our room , although not deluxe was fine anyway, and we really didn't realize it was not until checkout, when we went to tell the desk that breakfasts were billed to out room. They were removed immediately, and without hesitation, with a courteous and plausible explanation that when the reservations are not made through the Marriott system the details of the reservation and any requests, such as bed size, etc. are not transmitted to the hotel.Many Tripadvisor reviewers have commented negatively on the elevator system, and we were nervous about this. You enter the floor you wish to travel to on a keypad. An LCD display then tells you which car (A through G) will take you. If you are sight impaired, pressing a handicap symbol on the keypad causes the car letter to be voiced, and announcements made when the car opens and closes. The system worked very well when we were there, and was in fact quite fast. The staff indicated that when the hotel is completely full, it does struggle to keep up, but I suspect that when a 1300 room hotel is completely full, as I was told it will be next week for Mardi Gras, any hotel will have elevator delays.We only dined in the Cafe du Marche restaurant for breakfast. The buffet included an omelette station, smoked salmon, fine italian meats ( proscutto, salami, etc), bacon and sausage, grits and oatmeal, biscuits and gravy, cereals, bagels, muffins, etc. The quality was good and service attentive and friendly. The location on Canal street is excellent, immediately adjacent to the Quarter, away from the noise of Bourbon ( but only a two minute walk if that's what you're there for.) The streetcar stops right in front of the hotel, and we were only a few minutes walk to the French Market, Cafe du Monde ( beignets, yum). One airport related comment: if you are more than one in your party, don't bother with the airport shuttle. It is $13.00 per person. A cab into the city for 2 is a fixed $29.00 and there is no wait. After paying for the shuttle we wasted an hour waitng for the next one to show up. After repeated gentle reassurances for 45 minutes that the next one was 10 minutes out, I politely but firmly asked for and was given a refund. For an extra 3 dollars we did not have to traipse around from hotel to hotel getting dropped off.New Orleans is ready for the tourist. There is still a lot of rebuilding to do, but most everything you want to do or see is open and good to go, with one or two exceptions. In addition, you'll be able to get a table at the restaurant of your choice without as much difficulty.Laissez les bon temps roulez!  
<Date>Feb 14, 2007

<Author>chipbarfly
<Content>Great Location and Stay I stayed at the Marriott in January for a conference and was extremely happy with my selection. I had never been to New Orleans before so I was unsure as to which was the best location (considering Bourbon Street and Convention Center).With that in mind, it was an ideal location. I could walk easily to all of my locations.When I checked in (following a five hour delay in JFK), I asked for a room on a lower floor due to earlier comments about the elevators. The room was fine, but smaller than I had expected. I went back to the desk and politely asked for another room (I had originally requested a King) - I was given a wonderful room on the 32nd floor with great views of the river and downtown. The staff was very accommodating.The new elevator system worked well, I rarely waited more than a few minutes. Just remember there aren't any buttons on the inside!I ate most of my meals out, however, the food served at the bar was more than adequate and quite tasty.I would certainly stay here again.

<Author>lynn2
<Content>Great location We stayed at the hotel with our adult daughters, and were happy to help the New Orleans economy. The location was great - a little quieter, close to restaurants and a short walk to Bourbon Street. Our kids felt safe walking back and forth at night because there were a lot of people on the street at night. We didn't feel quite as confident, but didn't have any problems. The hotel does seem to be understaffed, but trying to do their best. The elevator system is ridiculous when the hotel is busy - we saw many people walking up to the 10th floor - with luggage. Allow plenty of time to get down to the lobby in the evening if you have to be somwhere. Options for eating in the hotel are limited and sometimes we were hungry and didn't feel like walking 4 blocks to a restaurant. Room service is listed as 24hrs, but it is not - that was pre-Katrina. Long lines for coffee in the morning. Comfortable beds in small rooms. The concierge got us a reservation one night at a restaurant we chose - Rainbow Grill, very busy and very good. Another night she chose a restaurant for us and made a great show of telling us how lucky we were to get a reservation anywhere and how busy and tired she was - then we got to the restaurant and it was almost empty.Things aren't perfect in New Orleans and it certainly wasn't our most comfortable vacation. But this city needs so much help and still has a lot to offer. We were happy to overlook a few annoyances and enjoyed our stay.

<Author>uncbones
<Content>Location, location, location!!! Spent New Year's weekend at the Marriott and loved the location. Within easy walking distance to RiverWalk, Canal Place Shops, and French Quarter/Bourbon Street. Decent accomodations with comfortable bed. Bathroom is small and without fan. Most frustrating for me was having to bend down to see my face in the bathroom mirror--I'm a little over 6'1, and could only see my chest when standing. Nice showerhead and toiletries. Avoid the lobby bar--$5.50 for a Mich Ultra. Walk down to Bourbon Street for cheap drinks, Pat O'Brien's $7 Hurricane well worth it! The bank of elevators work fine most of the time, but are overwhelmed with large crowds. You punch in your floor number and it tells you which of the eight elevators to take. On one occasion I ended up going to the 19th floor and then taking the stairs to the 21st. And then went down 21 flights to avoid having to fit in a full elevator going down. But this was a fully-booked weekend with Panthers/Saints game, New Year's eve parties, and Sugar Bowl crowds. Didn't really spend a whole lot of time in the room or exploring the hotel, but again was pleased with proximity to the French Quarter.

<Author>lcacsd
<Content>Terrible elevators, nice hotel While the New Orleans Marriott was indeed quite nice for a downtown Marriott - and I stay at many- the elevator situation when I was there for a conference earlier this week was intolerable. I actually walked up 30 floors - no kidding, and after a very long day of conference work - rather than wait in a 30+-minute line that stretched into the lobby. The staff indicated that this elevator gridlock happens often between 5 and 7 pm, or whenever there is any large number of people. Why? Their elevators use a new system where you punch in the floor you want (not just up or down), and the LED indicates which elevator will be coming for you (A through E); then when you get in, there are no buttons to push for your floor, the elevator goes there automatically. Thre are no light or floor indicators at the elevatorbanks on any floor, so you cannot tell where the elevator is, or which one is arriving. The staff told us that when there are many people waiting, and so enter their desired floor repeatedly (you know, like you push the up or down botton just to be sure when you've waited a while) the computer systems becomes confused and overwhelmed and the elevators slow down, stop on every floor, or just can't cope. A 15-minute wait was not unusual for people at our conference trying to get down from their rooms for dinner or meetings. People were often late as a result.Consequently I must caution against staying at this Marriott when you attend a convention or any busy time - or ask for a room on a low floor with no view and expect to walk both up and down. I personaly will never stay there again, although the staff were delightful, the room was lovely albeit somewhat small, and the food very good.

<Author>Black2001GT
<Content>The New Orleans Marriott is Back. The New Orleans Marriott is back in all her charm. This is a very old hotel but she shows her age well. The rooms are refurbished and the beds are very comfortable. The Bathrooms are a bit small. We had a wonderful view of the river from our 36th floor room. By using discount code I24, I received a rate of $99.00 per night, including a lavish breakfast buffet for 2.The Marriott is in a great location, at the foot of Canal Street. Harrah Casino, the ferry and the French Quarter are all within walking distance. My best friend and I were fortunate enough too had planned a visit to New Orleans at the same time and I had tickets to the Monday Night Saints vs Falcons football game so we decided to make a mini vacation out of the entire weekend. Even though we are New Orleans natives we wanted to stay downtown and take in the city like tourists. During the day we visited our family and spent allot of time in the casino and the French Quarter during the night.The Staff were all great as we were not the most accommodating guest. We stayed out pretty late and usually woke up in just enough time to partake in the delicious breakfast buffet, on 2 occasions, we slept right through breakfast. The concierge was knowledgeable when it came to recommending places to grab a late night bite. The exercise room has free weights, treadmills and elliptical machines. The elliptical machines and treadmills have flat screen TV on them so you could watch the news during your workout. There are also complementary headphones as you enter the exercise room.There are residential parts of the city that are still decimated and the New Orleans economy could really use a boost right now. Take some time during your vacation and visit New Orleans. Downtown, the CBD, the Garden District and the French Quarters are pretty much the same as they were pre-Katrina. Don let the media give you the wrong impression of the state of this great city.

<Author>RueStPeter718
<Content>Wonderful return to the Marriott! I visit NO 6-8 times a year and have done so for the better part of my adult life. Many of those visits over the years were spent at the Marriott. In more recent years, however, time was spent with friends who owned a BB.After the tragedy that was (and is) Katrina, I have returned to NO 5 times, re-learning some of the hotel offerings in the Quarter and CBD. By far, the Marriott has been the most enjoyable of these experiences. Clean, comfortable rooms, a great location (out one door and you're on Canal towards the CBD  casino; out another you're in the heart of the Quarter and only a block from ACME--yum), and a friendly, helpful staff.A dear friend of ours who is an NOFD Captain rode Katrina out here with his crew. He has some tales to tell of the fortress she was...and is.True to form, the Marriott on Canal remains a reliable and solid oasis for the weary traveler/reveler.

<Author>RiverCityLass
<Content>Great location but elevators were a nightmare We just returned from 5 nights at the New Orleans Marriott. All the staff we encountered were friendly and helpful. There are 3 Marriotts in the New Orelans area and two are on Canal Street less than a block apart. Be sure you know which one you are considering. I requested a corner room and it was larger than the standard rooms but was still on the small side. The bathrooms are very small and there is no vanity or sink or dressing area outside of the actual bathroom. For our family of four, this was a real drawback. Also, the steam from the shower or tub made it almost impossible to dry your hair and there was no wall mirror in the actual hotel room itself. I found this to be very inconvenient. The beds were wonderful-double sheeted, duvets rather than a bedspread-very nice. Housekeeping could have been better. The bathroom floor was not cleaned during our stay nor was the carpet vacumed.Our experience witht the breakfast buffet was not good. We found the hot food cold and the buffet line was not kept very well. At $16.00 each, it should have been much better. To be fair, they were extremely busy and appeared to be just overwhelmed. We ordered appetizers from the Lobby bar one evening and they were very good.The worst problem we had was with the elevators. 30 minute waits were not unusal. We missed a bus one evening because we couldn't get an elevator-we finally had to walk down from the 21st floor. It was a problem every day we were there and at all times of the day. It seemed like out of 8 elevators at the most 3 were working in the tower we stayed in.Over all it wasn't a bad stay but the hotel is not quite up to par with other Marriotts we've stayed at. Don't expect a 4 star hotel experience, but it is a solid 3. Would we stay there again-probably. The location is great and the staff seemed eager to please.  
<Date>Aug 8, 2005

<Author>bmarcus
<Content>Great hotel at reasonable rate I booked a room for a great rate on Priceline. After staying 5 nights at Hotel Monteleone my party and I went to Cajun country and needed a hotel to stay in New Orleans for one night again before our flight. The Mariott did not disappoint. I was just looking for a clean room but was surprised to find great workout facilities, a nice pool, a vibrant lobby, and a colorfully decorated room. THe elevators are slow and I did only stay there one night. I could see a negative of the hotel being its enormous size. At capacity the hotel probably feels very crowded and the elevators were slow even in our one-night off season stay. The location is good. You are not in the heart of the french quarter but at the edge of it on canal street. Canal street is a busy city street, not a great spot for a hotel entrance, but it's always bustling and as safe as any other big street in an urban center.All in all, after two stays at the Hotel Monteleone, I would consider booking my next stay in New Orleans at the Mariott. It did not disappoint.

<Author>QuarterDano
<Content>Great, but elevators are the SLOWEST EVER. I've stayed at the Marriott New Orleans on several different occasions for the past several years. The hotel rooms just keep getting better and better. The beds are phenomenal! The decorating is cool and modern, rooms very spacious. However, our rooms a/c vent was filthy and hanging out on one corner....not a great first impression. There are signs explaining how renovations are in progress and it should not bother your stay....how wrong they are! We were already awake, thank goodness, at 8:30 a.m. and heard a horrendously loud drill, grinding into the concrete above our room! This went on for at least 15 minutes (maybe longer since we left to go to breakfast). The WORST part of the stay is the elevators....we waited in a very long line for 10-15 minutes several different times for an elevator to arrive! We also saw staff using guest elevators to transport food, audio visual equipment, etc. instead of the freight elevator. Always great customer service, so just grin and bear the renovations!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>New Orleans best location We stayed at the New Orleans Marriott June 11-14th. Loved this hotel! Great room (River View) overlooking the Mississippi River. Location is perfect; 3 blocks from Bourbon St, 2 blocks from Harrahs Casino and Riverwalk, and the Garden district and museums are just to the right of Canal St.  You can't go wrong at any restaurant on Bourbon St. They are all great!Also, the entertainment is great, no matter what kind of music you like, you'll find it on Bourbon St. Just keep walking till you find what you like. Guaranteed you'll see plenty of sights on your way. We took the city tour, which helped us get our bearings in this great city, the Swamp (airboat) tour which was great fun and there are Ghost, Voodoo and Vampire tours available. We will return to New Orleans soon and will definitely stay at the Marriott. Weonly wish they had in room safes; they did have safe deposit boxes at the front desk at no charge which was great.

Although the location is excellent - only three streets from Bourbon Street - the service is horrible. I checked in to find someone elses socks left in the room by the maids. When the weekend maids clean the rooms they prop open the door to one room and crank the TV so they can hear it up and down the hall as they clean the other rooms with complete disregard for other guests still on the floor. I ordered room service and they cut me off several times to ask will that be all. They finally allowed me to complete my order and then they had to call me back to ask me questions about what I wanted and then still got it wrong!The room was small, but the bed was heaven. The bellmen are constantly in your face with their hands out. The location is really the only thing going for the hotel until they train their staff on customer service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel all around Stayed at the New Orleans Marriott 5/20-5/23. I had previously stayed at the Omni Royal Orleans which is also very nice. Marriott had a great location, walking distance to French Quarter, Riverwalk mall and Harrah's casino too. The room was very nice, looked like it had been remodeled. We stayed on the 37th floor and had a great view of the river. I heard almost everyone gets a river view. The hotel was also very quiet. I never heard loud people in the halls or other noises. We booked our hotel through a tour company, Northwest World Vacations and had a bit of a mix-up. The voucher I received was for 3 nights and that is what I had paid for but when I got to the hotel reservations only had me down for 2 nights. I was assured this wouldnt be a problem and they would fix it. 2 days later I went to use my key card to get into the room and it didnt work. I was worried the problem was not resolved but they sent up a secuirity officer who let us back in our room and gave us new keys and everything after that was fine. We did a gray line cemetery tour and a swamp tour with Cajun Encounters, both tour were great! The swamp tour is a must do! If you booked New Orleans Marriott-you wont be disappointed.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great for New Orleans! I have been to NO several times, but this was my first stay at Marriott. The location was sooo convenient to the Riverwalk, Harrah's, Bourbon Street, and Jackson Square. Literally in the middle of everything! The lobby to this hotel is gorgeous, and the staff were above and beyond friendly. I requested the River Tower, and they happily accomodated, even volunteering to find us the room with the best view of the river. Upon checkout, we used the Baggage room to store bags while we did more touring, and that was also handled seamlessly. The apparently newly decorated rooms included beds that were really gorgeous with lots of pillows, etc, and were extremely soft (although after 3 nights the cushiness was getting hard on my back!). Are the rooms smaller than 4 stars in other cities? Yep! Are the bathrooms smaller? Yep! Just like almost everything in New Orleans this is an older hotel with smaller rooms, but they do a wonderful job of making things homey, convenient, clean, and pretty. Really, after all, who goes to New Orleans to spend a lot of time in the rooms?? Also, in response to other posters who had bad experiences due to booking through a discount website, I too booked through Priceline, and this was not brought up once during our stay, nor did I feel like I got sub-par treatment due to this.My only complaint with this hotel is that all of the vending machines have Pepsi products ONLY. Yech!

<Author>rmarrs
<Content>Nice place THe New Orleans Marriott was a very nice place to stay during our recent trip to New Orleans with the Virginia Tech Football team. I was able to view 2 different rooms, including a double double and a suite. The suite was huge with separate living and sleeping rooms, and a full size bar. The double double was nice, but somewhat small, but had wonderful views of the city. The staff (except for the chief bellhop) were very friendly and able to help with just about everything. The hotel is about 3 blocks from Bourbon Street, but is centrally located in the city. About 25 minutes from the airport. I was able to eat at the hotel quite often, but it was a banquet style seating so special arrangements might have been made. The food was delicious either way.Nice place to stay, small regular rooms but huge suites, great location, and friendly service.

<Author>TorontoMao
<Content>okay if you booked through a discount website... I stayed at the NO Marriott beginning of March for 5 nights, attending a conference. The location is great (within walking distance to French Quarters, riverfront, Faubourg Marigny, etc) but not noisy at all. However, the room was small (1 king bed and there was very little room left in the room). Ventilation was a problem - the room felt damp even with the AC on full blast. We had to pay close to $10 a day for high speed internet, or, separately if in the lobby, for wireless internet, the connection for which was unreliable at best. Housekeeping was not great either - we found our ice bucket not dumped out or the glasses not cleaned or replaced. There was no water in all of the hotel during one of the days we stayed (for about 6 hours). For the price we paid which was the conference rate (supposedly better than rack rate), we'd expect more.

<Author>MardiGras05
<Content>Nice Hotel Had a good stay here for the last weekend of Mardi Gras. The front desk staff and other staff members I came in contact with were all friendly and helpful. The location of the hotel is excellent and is especially so during Mardi Gras because it is on the French Quarter side of Canal St., which eliminates the problem of trying to cross Canal St. when the parades are rolling. The hotel restaurant, gift shop, lobby bar and Canal St. bar are really convenient during inclimate weather or when you just don't feel like leaving the hotel. The room was your standard size room and everything was in working order. However, the beds were somewhat strange to sleep on as the mattress had a tendency to slide on the boxspring if you moved too much. I didn't have any problems sleeping on the bed, but I woke up a couple of times with part of the mattress hanging over the boxspring. Overall, I really liked my stay here and would definitely stay here again if the price is reasonable.

<Author>Lee4
<Content>Great Stay! Stayed here for one night on 7/23/04 with a priceline bid of $50.00, plus $24.00 for valet parking. I called a few days before arrival to request a king bed, non smoking room and it was ready upon arrival. The staff are all very friendly, from the front desk clerk to the bellmen and valets (even when they are not helping you). The hotel is busy, but it was always easy to catch an elevator. The location makes it easy to walk to the French Quarter and other locations along Canal Street and the Riverwalk area. With valet parking, you have in and out privileges at no charge, and it was easy to use this service. There is a coffee bar/cafe type place in the lobby that sold breakfast pastries, krispy kreme do-nuts, starbucks coffee, etc. if you do not want to leave the hotel (it's really easy to walk to Cafe du Monde, though!).The room itself was clean and comfortable--the bed was extremely comfortable with lots of pillows. All NO hotel rooms are small, but I thought this one was fine for 2 adults, especially when you are not in the room for long periods of time anyway. The bathroom was also clean and had Neutrogena products and a regular blow dryer, rather than those little, tiny ones that quit soon after you start using them. I'd be happy to stay here again.
